+Jamison Brereton

92
Dawn (1тАУ15), A┼Ыvins (16тАУ18)
Gotama R─Бh┼лgaс╣Зa
18 verses: jagat─л 1тАУ4, triс╣гс╣нubh 5тАУ12, uс╣гс╣Зih 13тАУ18
This metrically complex structure with two different dedicands must originally have consisted of several independent hymnsтАФprobably, with Oldenberg, verses 1тАУ4, 5тАУ8, 9тАУ12, 13тАУ15, 16тАУ18, all but the last dedicated to Dawn. Indeed, the first two segments (vss. 1тАУ4 in jagat─л, 5тАУ8 in triс╣гс╣нubh) appear to be partial variants of each other, the first describing multiple Dawns (except vs. 4), the second a single Dawn. There are precise agreements in lexicon, phraseology, and imagery, particularly between verses 1тАУ2 and 5тАУ6, that go beyond standard shared Dawn vocabulary. The seductive dancing girl of verse 4 also reminds of the smiling siren of verse 6. The third segment (vss. 9тАУ12) has fewer connections with the first two, but is themati cally unified, especially by the emphasis on тАЬdiminishing/belittlingтАЭ (all expressed by the root m─л in different combinations) in verses 10тАУ12.
All three of the segments in trimeter meter (that is, through vs. 12) contain arrest ing images, and the poet enjoys exploiting ambiguities to poetic effect. In verses 1 and 12, for example, he uses different syntactic constructions in the simile and the frame because the verb held in common by both can be either reflexive or transitive; in verse 3 the pun inherent in the root arc (both тАЬshineтАЭ and тАЬchantтАЭ) allows the introduction of a simile involving female work-songs, though the dawns themselves are presumably not chanting.
The last two segments, in uс╣гс╣Зih meter, to Dawn and the A┼Ыvins respectively (vss. 13тАУ15, 16тАУ18), are, not surprisingly, less complex. Both hope for the arrival of the divinities at the sacrifice, accompanied by plenty of presents.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Dawn As indicated in the published introduction, vss. 1-4 and 5-8 appear to be parallel hymns, the first with multiple Dawns, the second with just one.

( рдирд┐рд░реБ. резреи. рен) рдЗрддрд┐ рее рдЕрдХреНрд░рдд ред рдХрд░реЛрддреЗрд░реНрд▓реБрдЩрд┐ ’ рдордиреНрддреНрд░реЗ рдШрд╕ ’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреНрд▓реЗрдГ рд▓реБрдХреН ред +Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThese divinities of the morning have spread light (over the world); they make manifest the light in the eastern portion of the firmament, brightening all things, like warriors burnishing their weapons; the radiant and progressing mothers (of the earth), they travel daily (on their course).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Uс╣г─Бsaс╕е (plural): allusion to divinities that preside over the morning; Y─Бska notes that the plural is used honorifically (Nirukta 12.7); progressed mothers: m─Бtс╣Ы = maker, author; bh─Бso nirm─Бtryaс╕е: authors of light (Nirukta 12.7)

+Jamison Brereton

These very Dawns have made themselves a beacon. In the eastern half of the dusky realm they anoint their beam [=sacrificial post].
Presenting themselves, as bold ones present arms, the reddish cows, the mothers come toward (us).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In p─Бda a my tr. differs slightly from the standard ones. I suggest that the dawns have transformed themselves into a beacon, while in the standard interpr. they have created/manufactured a beacon for themselves.

In b following Proferes 2003 (JAOS 123, pp. 330-31), I suggest, on the basis of the fuller expression in the parallel verse 5c, that their тАЬbeamтАЭ is being anointed like the sacrificial post (sv├бru-) at a ritual.

In c the poet exploits the syntactic ambiguity of the middle participle niс╣гkс╣Ыс╣Зv─Бn├б-. In the frame he takes it as a reflexive, тАЬpresenting themselves,тАЭ but in the simile it is transitive тАЬpresenting arms.тАЭ The middle voice is still justified, however, because the weapons belong to the subjects of the participle.

+Griffith

THESE Dawns have raised their banner; in the eastern half of the mid-air they spread abroad their shining light.
Like heroes who prepare their weapons for the war, onward they come bright red in hue, the Mother Cows.

+Geldner

Dort haben die Morgenr├╢ten ihr Banner aufgesteckt, auf der ├╢stlichen Seit des Raums legen sie sich Licht als Salbe auf, sich abl├╢send wie Tapfere ihre Waffen wechseln. Es kehren die roten K├╝he wieder, die M├╝tter.

+Grassmann

Schon haben diese Morgenr├╢then Licht gebracht, und schm├╝cken in des Raumes Osten sich mit Glanz, Wie k├╝hne Helden sich versehn mit Waffenschmuck; wie Mutterk├╝he nahen nun die rothen sich.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe feminine le leaders (of the morning) illuminate with their inherent radiance the remotest parts (of the heaven), with a simultaneous effort, like warriors (with their shining arms in the van of battle), bringing every kind of food to the performer of good works, to the bountiful, and to the worshipper who presents libations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Arcanti = lit. worship; i.e. illuminate the heavens, spreading over or extending; like warriors: the comparison is explained: ‘as they spread with bright arms along the front of the array, so the rays of the dawn spread along the sky before the coming of the sun’

+Jamison Brereton

They chant [/shine] like women busy with their labors, (coming always) along the same route from afar,
conveying refreshment to the man of good action [=sacrificer], the man of good gifts, the man who sacrifices and presses soma all the days.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard tr. are in agreement that ├бrcanti only means тАЬthey singтАЭ here and that the meaning тАШshineтАЩ for this verb stem is dubious. This judgment seems short- sighted and unresponsive to the poetics of this hymn, and even if тАШshineтАЩ is not the normal sense of ├бrca-, the nominal derivatives like arc├н(s)- тАШray, flameтАЩ (see arc├нs- in 5a) would allow a тАШshineтАЩ sense under the proper circumstances. And these are the proper circumstances. This verse-initial verb, following on two verses describing the color, brightness, and beams of the dawns, would most naturally be interpreted with a тАШshineтАЩ sense. The simile that follows, involving women at work, would then cause the audience to rethink this assumption, producing the interpretation тАШsingтАЩ, with the women singing work songs at their labors. But тАШsingтАЩ makes little sense for the frame of the passage: do dawns тАШsingтАЩ? While тАШshineтАЩ makes little sense for the simile: do working women тАШshineтАЩ? As in 1c the poet uses the ambiguity of the verbal pivot to craft two incompatible but verbally impeccable pictures, but this time he relies not on syntactic ambiguity as in 1c but synonymity – a pun on the verbal root underlying the verb form. The pun may be even cleverer than so far presented. Although the primary sense of ├бrcanti for the dawns should be тАШshineтАЩ, it is possible that there is a secondary sense тАШsingтАЩ, in that birds begin to sing at dawn and the ritual recitation also begins at that time. Similarly, although тАШsingтАЩ should be the primary sense for the women in the simile, they may also be said to shine if they are glistening with sweat from their labors. (Recall the old expression тАЬmen sweat, but women тАШglow.тАЩтАЭ) It should be noted that Ludwig thought the verb was тАЬdoppelsinnigтАЭ (see Geldner n. 3a).

In terms of the published translation (and other standard tr.), the simile particle n├б is late, since the simile is assumed to start with n─Б╠Бr─лс╕е. However, it is possible that n─Б╠Бr─лс╕е characterizes the Dawns, and the simile consists only of ap├бso n├б viс╣гс╣н├нbhiс╕е. In that case, the chanting workers could be men: an alt. tr. тАЬThe ladies chant [/shine] like workers at their labors.тАЭ Pace Grassmann and Lubotsky, ├бha should be taken not as the particle, but as short neut. pl.

to ├бhar / ├бhan- тАШdayтАЩ, with v├н┼Ыv─Б; cf. the well-attested expression ├бh─Б v├н┼Ыv─Б.

+Griffith

They sing their song like women active in their tasks, along their common path hither from far away,
Bringing refreshment to the liberal devotee, yea, all things to the worshipper who pours the juice.

+Geldner

Sie stimmen den Lobgesang an, gleich Frauen flei├Яig an der Arbeit, in ein und derselben Fahrt aus der Ferne kommend, indem sie alle Tage dem Werkfrommen und Freigebigen, dem Soma bereitenden Opferer Labsal zuf├╝hren.

+Grassmann

Wie Frauen, fleissig bei der Arbeit, strahlen sie, auf gleichem Wege ziehend aus der Ferne her, Dem gabenreichen Frommen bringend Labetrunk, an jedem Tag dem Opferer, der Soma braut.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬUс╣гas cuts off the accusative ulated (glooms), as a barber (cuts off the hair); she bares her bosom as a cow yields her udder (to the milker); and, as cattle hasten to their pastures, she speeds to the east, and shedding light upon all the world, dissipates the darkness.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Nс╣Ыt┼лr iva, like a barber;

Nс╣Ыt┼лс╕е = a dancing-girl; alternative reading: uс╣гas displays graces, like a dancing-girl (pe┼Ыaс╣Гsi vapate, to cut off or possess either darkness or elegance)

+Jamison Brereton

She strews ornaments on herself like a dancing girl. She uncovers her breast like a ruddy (cow) her udder [?].
Making light for all creation, Dawn has opened up the darkness as cows (would) their pen.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

b├бrjaha- in b is a hapax, but related to dual barjahy├и in AV XI.8.14 in a list of body parts, found between the ribs and the sides. Whitney/Lanman tr. тАШnipplesтАЩ there.

The consensus tr. тАШudderтАЩ seems reasonable, esp. on the assumption that usr─Б╠БтАШruddyтАЩ designates a cow. However, the purport of the simile is a little unclear. Since cows donтАЩt wear clothes, their udders are not covered to begin with and uncovering is unnecessary. Geldner suggests that the simile is proleptic: DawnтАЩs breast becomes as visible as a cowтАЩs full udder, but this interpretation requires that the verb (тАШuncoversтАЩ) that should mediate between frame and simile has been semantically elided.

The simile in d is similarly тАЬoff,тАЭ since cows donтАЩt have the capacity to open their own pens. Macdonell (Hymns from the Rigveda, 1922) tr. тАЬas when cows break from their stalls,тАЭ which makes more sense, but again misrepresents the pivotal verb.

The apparently wrong sandhi ─Бvar t├бmaс╕е is, as has long been known, an ex. of degemination in context: ─Бvar represents the older 3rd sg. root aor. *─Бvart. See Oldenberg, Prol. 424 n. 1, AiG I.304-5, 336.

+Griffith

She, like a dancer, puts her broidered garments on: as a cow yields her udder so she bares her breast.
Creating light for all the world of life, the Dawn hath laid the darkness open as the cows their stall.

+Macdonell

She throws gay garments round her like a dancing girl; E’en as a cow her udder, she displays her breast. Creating light for all the world, Dawn has unbarred The gates of darkness as when cows break from their stall.

+Grassmann

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHer brilliant light is first seen towards (the east); it spreads and disperses the thick darkness; she anoints her beauty as the priests anoint the sacrificial food in sacrifices; the daughter of the sky awaits the glorious sun.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Duhit─Б divaс╕е, the daughter of heaven or the sky

+Jamison Brereton

Her gleaming ray has appeared opposite. She spreads herself out, thrusts away the black void.
The Daughter of Heaven has propped up her bright beam, her
ornament, like (a priest) propping up the sacrificial post, the
ornament at the ceremonies, and anointing it.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

As noted before, vs. 5 seems to match vs. 1 and begin a new hymn parallel to vss. 1-4, but adapted for a single dawn, not the multiples in vs. 1. The return of the words bh─Бn├║- тАШbeamтАЩ and тИЪa├▒j тАШanointтАЩ (1b) is particularly salient, as also тИЪ┼Ыri (2d), тИЪarc (3a), and p├й┼Ыas- (4a).

The poet produces yet another complication of simile structure in cd. The Daughter of Heaven in d is clearly the subject of the clause, but the simile occupying c has a participle in the masc. nom. sg., a├▒j├бn, which cannot modify the grammatical subject. We must here supply a masculine ritual officiant, who is propping up and anointing the sacrificial post, as Dawn props up and anoints her beam. (Note that bh─Бn├║m served as object of both verbs in the earlier parts of the hymn: 1b bh─Бn├║m a├▒jate, 2d bh─Бn├║m тАж a┼Ыi┼Ыrayuс╕е.) The two distinct objects in simile and frame are mediated by the word p├й┼Ыas-, which is appropriate to both. Dawn has just donned her own p├й┼Ы─Бс╣Гsi in 4a, but p├й┼Ыas- can also be used of ritual paraphernalia – e.g., the pressing stones, which are called adhvar├бsya p├й┼Ыaс╕е at VII.42.1.

+Griffith

We have beheld the brightness of her shining; it spreads and drives away the darksome monster.
Like tints that deck the Post at sacrifices, Heaven’s Daughter hath attained her wondrous splendour.

+Macdonell

Her radiant shimmer has appeared before us; It spreads, and drives away the swarthy monster. As one anoints the post at sacrifices The daughter of the sky extends her lustre.

+Geldner

Ihr heller Schein ist wieder sichtbar geworden; sie breitet sich aus, vertreibt das schwarze Ungeheuer. Die Himmelstochter hat ihr buntes Licht aufgesetzt wie der Priester bei den Opfern den Pfosten aufsetzt, indem er ihm bunte Farben aufsalbt.

+Grassmann

Es hat sich jetzt gezeigt ihr helles Leuchten, sie bricht hervor, verjagt das schwarze Grausen, Des Himmels Tochter breitet helles Licht aus, ihr Kleid bemalend wie beim Fest den Pfosten.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWe have crossed over the boundary of darkness. Uс╣гas restores the consciousness (of living beings); bright-shining, she smiles, like a flatterer to obtain favour, and, lovely in all her radiance, she has swallowed, for our delight the darkness.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

We have crossed to the further shore of this darkness. Dawn, dawning, is making her patterns.
Like one aiming to please, she, shining forth, smiles for splendor. She of the lovely face has awakened (us?) to benevolence.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

vay├║n─Б kс╣Ыс╣Зoti reprises ├бkran тАж vay├║n─Бni in 2c.

ch├бndaс╕е is somewhat problematic. Grassmann takes it as a masc. nom. sg. to a them.

adj. ch├бnda-, with the developed sense тАЬder Gefallende, Schmeichler oder Buhle,тАЭ and this tack is followed by the standard tr. (incl. the published one). But the only other supposed occurrence of this stem, in VIII.7.36, I take to the much better established s-stem neut. ch├бndas- тАШmetrical vs.тАЩ. However, that solution is not available here, at least as far as I can see, and so I reluctantly follow the standard solution, without much faith in its correctness. It does not help this interpr. that Dawn is being compared to a masc. being, esp. since smiling is almost always a feminine action.

Redupl. aj─лgaс╕е must be a transitive redupl. aor. beside j─Б╠Жrayati тАШcauses to awakenтАЩ. Cf. I.113.4-6: uс╣г─Б╠Бaj─лgar bh├║van─Бni v├н┼Ыv─Б. I supply тАШusтАЩ as obj. here, on the basis of the 1st pl. subj. in p─Бda a.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe brilliant daughter of the sky, the exciter of plural asant voices, is praised by the descendants of Gotama. Uс╣гas, grant us food associated with progeny and dependants, and distinguished by horses and cattle.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Light-filled leader of liberalities, the Daughter of Heaven is praised by the Gotamas.
O Dawn, mete out prizes rich in offspring, rich in men, founded on horses, tipped with cows.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the etymological, though no longer semantic, relationship between s┼лnс╣Ы╠Бt─Бn─Бm (a) and nс╣Ыv├бtaс╕е (c).

+Griffith

The Gotamas have praised Heaven’s radiant Daughter, the leader of the charm of pleasant voices.
Dawn, thou conferrest on us strength with offspring and men, conspicuous with kine and horses.

+Macdonell

The radiant leader of rich gifts, the daughter Of Heaven by the Gotamas is lauded. Mete out to us, O Dawn, largesses: offspring, Brave men, conspicuous wealth in cows and horses.

+Geldner

Als glanzvolle Bringerin der Schenkungen wird die Tochter des Himmels von den Gotamas gepriesen. Teil uns Belohnungen zu, in Kindern und M├дnnern bestehend, wobei Rosse den Schlu├Я und Rinder die Spitze bilden, o Usas!

+Grassmann

Gepriesen wird die helle Freudenbotin, des Himmels Tochter, von den Gotamiden; O schenk uns Wohlstand, der an Ross und Rindern, an Kindern, M├дnnern reich sei, Morgenr├╢the!

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay I obtain, Uс╣гas, that ample wealth with confers fame, posterity, troops of slaves, and is characterized by horses; which you, who abount in riches and are the giver of food, display, (when gratified) by hymns and holy sacrifices.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

O Dawn, might I attain this glorious wealth, rich in good heroes, founded on horses, with alien-slaves as its forelockтАФ
o you of good portion, who with fame of wondrous power radiate
forth, motivated by (desire for) the prize, to lofty (wealth).

+Jamison Brereton Notes

тАШForelockтАЩ for pravarga- may seem slightly flippant, but I wanted to capture the тАШtwistтАЩ sense of pr├б тИЪvс╣Ыj, in contrast to the anodyne тАШhaving slaves at the frontтАЩ found in the other tr.

The final bс╣Ыh├бntam of d obviously refers back to the ray├нm so carefully detailed in ab, but is separated from that phrase by a considerable amount of material. Rather than making it a long-delayed part of that NP I have taken it as a pseudo-goal with vibh─Б╠Бsi, with v─Б╠Бja-pras┼лt─Б giving grounds for that goal.

+Griffith

O thou who shinest forth in wondrous glory, urged onward by thy strength, auspicious Lady,
Dawn, may I gain that wealth, renowned and ample, in brave sons, troops of slaves, far-famed for horses.

+Macdonell

May I attain that wealth renowned and ample, With many heroes, troops of friends, and horses, O Dawn, that shinest forth with wondrous glory. Urged on by mighty strength, auspicious lady.

Lass, Morgenr├╢the, mich das Gut erlangen, das reich ergl├дnzt an Helden, Rossen, Knechten, Die du durch Ruhm und Heldenthat erstrahlest, zu grosser Gabe angeregt, o sel’ge.

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe divine (Uс╣гas), having lighted up the whole world, spreads, expanding with her radiance, towards the west, arousing all living creatures to their labours; she hears the speech of all endowed with thought.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The goddess, overseeing all creatures, (like) an eye, facing toward them, shines forth widely.
Awakening all life to activity, she has found the speech of every
zealous one.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Unfortunately it is not possible to render the three fronted forms of v├н┼Ыva- (p─Бdas a, c, d) in non-awkward English.

c├бkс╣гuс╕е in b can be either nom. or acc. Most tr. take it as the latter, with Dawn facing either the eye(s) of, presumably, humans (so Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н], Renou) or the eye of the sun (so Macdonell [Hymns from the Rigveda], Maurer). The latter is unlikely on pragmatic grounds: although the eye of the sun is a standard trope in the RV (see in fact 11d), the sun rises after dawn, and Dawn surely wouldnтАЩt be looking behind her, to the east. The former is certainly possible, but I prefer to take c├бkс╣гuс╕е as nominative, referring to Dawn as an eye, since she has just been said to oversee (abhic├бkс╣гy─Б) all creatures.

IтАЩm not entirely sure what p─Бda d refers to, but perhaps it means that by dawning she has stimulated ritual speech and therefore тАЬfindsтАЭ it.

+Griffith

Bending her looks on all the world, the Goddess shines, widely spreading with her bright eye westward.
Waking to motion every living creature, she understands the voice of each adorer.

+Macdonell

Looking on all created things, the goddess Shines far and wide, facing the eye of S┼лrya. Awaking every living soul to motion, She has aroused the voice of every thinker.

+Geldner

Alle Gesch├╢pfe ├╝berschauend erstrahlt die G├╢ttin weithin, jedem Auge zugewandt. Alles was lebt zum Gehen erweckend hat sie die Rede eines jeden Dichtenden gefunden;

+Grassmann

Die G├╢ttin, alle Wesen rings beschauend, erstrahlet weit, ihr Auge zu uns wendend, Zum Wandern alles, was da lebt erweckend, hat jedes frommen S├дngers Lied belauscht sie.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe divine and ancient Uс╣гas, born again and again and bright with unchanging hues, wastes away the life of a mortal, like the wife of a hunter cutting up and dividing the birds.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъvaghn─л = lit. wife of a dog-killer, explained as vy─Бdhastr─л

+Jamison Brereton

Being born again and again though ancient, (always) beautifying herself to the same hue,
like a successful (gambler) with the best throw who diminishes the stake (of his opponent), the goddess keeps diminishing the lifetime of the mortal as she ages him.

+Griffith

Ancient of days, againagain born newly, decking her beauty with the self-same raiment.
The Goddess wastes away the life of mortals, like a skilled hunter cutting birds in pieces.

+Macdonell

Born newly again and again though ancient, Herself adorning with the selfsame colour, The goddess wears away the life of mortals, Like stakes diminished by a skilful gambler.

+Geldner

Die uralte, immer wieder geborene G├╢ttin, die sich in der gleichen Farbe geputzt, alt machend und die Lebenszeit des Sterblichen vermindernd wie der geschickte Gl├╝cksspieler die schlechten W├╝rfe.

+Grassmann

Die alte G├╢ttin, immer neu geboren, ergl├дnzend immer mit derselben Farbe; Wie seine W├╝rfel birgt der schlaue Spieler, so l├дsst das Leben sie des Menschen altern

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬShe has been seen illuminating the boundaries of the sky, and driving into disappearance the spontaneously-retiring (night); wearing away the ages of the human race, she shines with light like the bride of the sun.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Svas─Бram = svayam sarantim, going to her own accord (night);

J─Бra = causer of the decay of night, explained as S┼лrya

+Jamison Brereton

Uncovering the ends of heaven, she has awakened. She keeps her sister [=Night] far away.
Diminishing human (life-)spans, the maiden radiates forth with the eye of her swain [=Sun].

+Griffith

She hath appeared discovering heaven’s borders: to the far distance she drives off her Sister.
Diminishing the days of human creatures, the Lady shines with all her lover’s splendour.

+Macdonell

The ends of heaven disclosing, she awakens; To distance far she banishes her sister. Diminishing the years of life, the maiden Flushes afar with the light of her lover.

+Geldner

Des Himmels Enden enth├╝llend ist sie erwacht; sie treibt die Schwester weit fort. Die menschlichen Lebenszeiten schm├дlernd erstrahlt die junge Frau mit dem Auge ihres Buhlen.

+Grassmann

Sie ist erwacht, des Himmels Rand enth├╝llend, und ihre Schwester treibt sie in die Ferne; Aufreibend stets die menschlichen Geschlechter, erstrahlt die Jungfrau in dem Blick des Buhlen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe affluent and adorable Uс╣гas has sent her rays abroad, as (a cowherd drives) the cattle (to pasture), and spreads expansive, like flowing water; she is beheld associated with the rays of the sun, unimpeding sacred ceremonies.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Aminat─л daivy─Бni vrat─Бni = not injuring, i.e. favouring, divine rites to the gods, which are to be performed by daylight (after dawn): na r─Бtrau na s─Бyam asti dev─Бya ajuс╣гс╣нam = sacrifice is not acceptable to the gods at night, or in the evening (RV. 5.77.2)

+Jamison Brereton

The bright, well-portioned one spreading herself as if (dispersing) cattle, like a river (spreading) its surge, she has whitened forth widely. Not belittling the divine commandments, she has come into view,
appearing along with the rays of the sun.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

This last verse of the trimeter portion of the hymn plays more tricks with simile structure. In p─Бda a prath─Бn─Б╠Бfunctions like niс╣гkс╣Ыс╣Зv─Бn─Б╠Бin 1c; that is, it has both reflexive and transitive values. In the frame it is reflexive (тАЬspreading herselfтАЭ), in my view, though Geldner, Renou, Macdonell, Maurer all supply тАЬraysтАЭ as the object, on no contextual grounds. (However, Geldner does allow for the reflexive possibility in his notes 12a, 1c.) In the simile pa┼Ы┼л╠Бn is the object; the assumed subject might be тАЬcowherdтАЭ or the like (so tentatively Renou). But the simile is quite appropriate to Dawn for two reasons: first, it is often said that livestock go out to pasture at dawn and return to the fold at night; second, the rays of Dawn are often referred to as cows (see in fact vs. 2 above), and though I donтАЩt think the stem pa┼Ы├║- is so used, it inhabits the same semantic space as the more usual terms that participate in this metaphor.

The second simile, s├нndhur n├б kс╣г├│daс╕е in b, is taken by Geldner, Renou, Macdonell, Maurer with the verb of b, vy ├а┼Ыvait. Because this verb тАШwhitenedтАЩ is intransitive, this requires either taking kс╣г├│daс╕е adverbially (Renou тАЬcomme le fleuve (en son) remousтАЭ) or construing s├нndhuс╕е тАж kс╣г├│daс╕е as a loose compound (Geldner тАЬwie die StromflotтАЭ).

Although either is possible, the syntactic difficulties disappear if the simile falls within the verbal domain of prath─Бn─Б╠Б, тАЬlike a river spreading its surge.тАЭ Given this poetтАЩs particular delight in manipulating similes, it is entirely in character to end this section of the hymn with a triple play.

Witzel Got┼Н interpret the similes more or less as I do.

P─Бda c is structurally parallel with 11c, using the same verb m─л тАШdiminish, belittleтАЩ, though here in the negative (11c praminat─л╠Б, 12c ├бminat─л), both playing off ─Бmin─Бn─Б╠Бin 10c. The relationship between 11c and 12c is particularly close, with the human and the divine playing off each other: 11c praminat─л╠Бmanuс╣гy─Б╠Бyug─Б╠Бni, 12c ├бminat─л da├нvy─Бni vrat─Б╠Бni.

+Griffith

The bright, the blessed One shines forth extending her rays like kine, as a flood rolls his waters.
Never transgressing the divine commandments, she is beheld visible with the sunbeams.

+Macdonell

Gracious and bright, spreading her rays like cattle, As a river its flood, afar she glimmers. Infringing not the gods’ unchanging statutes, She flushes radiant with the beams of S┼лrya.

+Geldner

Ihre Strahlen wie die Rinder ausbreitend ist die Farbenpr├дchtige Holde weithin ergl├дnzt wie die Stromflut. Die g├╢ttlichen Gebote nicht schm├дlernd, l├д├Яt sie sich sehen mit den Strahlen des Sonnegottes erscheinend.

+Grassmann

Die helle, sel’ge leuchtet, ihre Strahlen wie Heerden breitend, wie das Meer die Wogen, Nie weichend von der gottgesetzten Ordnung, erschien sie sichtbar durch der Sonne Strahlen.

English translation:

+Jamison Brereton

You two, who have made your signal-call (reach) all the way to heaven and at the same time made light for the people,
convey nourishment here to us, you A┼Ыvins.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

GautamaтАЩs penchant for clever exploitation of syntactic possibilties returns in this verse, after a series of unremarkable Uс╣гс╣Зih verses (13-16). The verb in b, cakr├бthuс╕е, by my interpretation takes two different types of predicates and exhibits slightly different root meanings: in p─Бda a тАЬmake your call to heaven,тАЭ that is, make the call reach heaven; in b тАЬmake, i.e., create, light.тАЭ I am in agreement with the standard tr. of p─Бda b, but diverge from them in a, where Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) supply a separate verb (тАЬerhebtтАЭ) to govern ┼Ыl├│kam and interpret ─Б╠Бdiv├бс╕е temporally (тАЬzu dieser Stunde des TagesтАЭ), not spatially. Although ─Б╠Бdiv├бс╕е is sometimes used temporally (e.g., in the expression tr├нr ─Б╠Бdiv├бс╕е), I take the ─Б╠Бhere in the meaning тАЬall the way toтАЭ (GrassmannтАЩs тАЬPraep. mit folgendem Abl. тАж bis an, bis hin (r├дumlich)тАЭ). This usage of ─Б╠Бwas prepared for in the immediately preceding vs., 16a asm├бd ─Б╠БтАЬall the way to usтАЭ (though in opposite order). For a closely parallel expression, in a Dawn hymn, cf. III.61.4 ─Б╠Бnt─Бd [i.e., ─Б╠Б├бnt─Бd] div├бс╕е … ─Б╠Бprthivy ╠е ─Б╠Бс╕е тАЬall the way to the end of heaven and of earth.тАЭ For the ┼Ыl├│ka- reaching heaven, cf. I.83.6, 190.4, and for ┼Ыl├│kam as object of тИЪkс╣Ы, IV.53.3.
